§ 54.01 LICENSES.
   (A)   To receive a local septage license, waste hauler shall submit a copy
of the state permit and $50, local license fee payable to the Town of Topeka
Wastewater, c/o Town Clerk, 124 E. Lake Street, PO Box 127, Topeka, IN 46571.
The local license is valid for one calendar year and must be renewed every May.
   (B)   It is the septage waste hauler's responsibility to provide the
Wastewater Utility with updated information within 15 days of a change in
ownership, address, phone number, authorized vehicle, IDEM business permit, or
any other similar information related to their waste hauling business.
   (C)   The Wastewater Utility will not accept any hauled waste from any
person or business until we have received evidence that a valid wastewater
management permit has been issued by the solid waste permit section of the
Indiana Department Environmental Management Office of Land Quality (IDEM OLQ)
and a valid hauler license from the Town Clerk's office has been obtained. A
state permit can be obtained by submitting an application for septage
management business permit (state form 50399) to the Office of Land Quality
(IDEM OLQ). The phone number for the solid waste permit section is (317)-232-
4473.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.02 CUSTOMER INVOICE REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   In accordance with 327 IAC 7.1-6-1(3), septage waste haulers must
provide their customer with a completed, legible invoice showing the following:
      (1)   The customer's name and address.
      (2)   The date the customer's sewage disposal system (or grease trap) was
cleaned.
      (3)   The amount of wastewater removed from the system in gallons.
   (B)   The invoice must bear the following:
      (1)   The name and address of business.
      (2)   The wastewater management state permit number.
      (3)   The license number of the vehicle used in cleaning the customer's
sewage disposal system.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.03 RECORDS RETENTION REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   State law 327 IAC 7.1-3-3 requires waste haulers to keep accurate
records of activities including:
      (1)   The contract or invoices for all wastewater service activities;
      (2)   The date, location, and method of disposal of wastewater associated
with each service (327 IAC 7.1-6-1(b)); and
      (3)   Land application records as required by 327 IAC 7.1-8-7, if
applicable.
   (B)   Such records must be:
      (1)   Located at the permitted wastewater management business address;
      (2)   Made available during normal business hours for inspection (I.C.
13-14-2-2);
      (3)   Updated weekly (except as required at 327 IAC 7.l-8-7(a)(5)); and
      (4)   Maintained for at least five years.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.04 WASTEWATER UTILITY BILLING AND PAYMENTS.
   (A)   The disposal fee for septic tank and waste originally was set at $0.06
per gallon and effective May 1, 2024 shall be set at $0.10 per gallon when
delivered by a registered waste hauler.
   (B)   The Wastewater Utility will provide a flow meter at the disposal
location. If the flow meter is not functioning properly or if the hauler is
asked to deliver the wastewater to a different location that is not metered,
the hauler will be billed based on the tank capacity or estimated volume based
on the visible volume of waste in the sight glass of the delivery truck.
   (C)   Billing statements are prepared and mailed on a monthly basis.
Payments are due and payable during the following month. A 10% late penalty
will be added to the bill for each month that the balance is not paid in full
by the due date. Any account that is delinquent for 90 days or more will be
referred to the attorney's office for collection and the acceptance of any
further waste loads will be denied. IDEM OLQ will be notified of any suspension
or revocation. The waste hauler will be responsible for all costs of
collection.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.05 DELIVERY LOCATIONS AND DATES.
   (A)   Septic loads can be disposed at the wastewater treatment facility
between from 7:00 a.m. to 2:30 p.m., five days per week. The driver should
arrive at least 15 minutes prior to the closing time to fill out paperwork,
collect a sample, and off-load the waste hauler’s holding tank before the
facility closes. If the delivery location changes for any reason, the company
will be notified by phone, as the changes occur.
   (B)   Drivers must contact a Wastewater Utility plant operator before
arriving at the disposal location. Drivers may call either of these numbers:
primary operator mobile phone (260)-350-1660, secondary phone (219)-207-5173.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.06 ACCEPTABLE WASTE TYPES.
   As a designated representative of the waste hauling company, the delivery
driver must certify that the information they have provided on the delivery
receipt paperwork is true, accurate and complete to the best of their knowledge
and belief and that the load does not contain any prohibited wastes. Falsifying
information on the delivery confirmation receipt may lead to suspension or
revocation of the company's disposal privileges. All loads are subject to
verification; therefore, each component of the load must be listed and
verifiable upon request by a copy of a dated customer receipt showing origin,
nature, and volume of waste. Grease trap waste is not accepted. No mixed loads
allowed. No industrial wastewater will be accepted without prior approval.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.07 UNLOADING PROCESS.
   (A)   A sample bottle will be provided for each truck delivering waste for
disposal. Drivers must collect a sample of the waste from the truck and bring
it to the attendant on duty before off-loading the vehicle. The attendant will
test the pH while the driver is filling out the required receipt and report
forms. Once the pH has been determined to be within the range of 5.0 to 10.0,
the driver may proceed to the unloading area. If load is outside the acceptable
pH range the load will be rejected and the driver will not be allowed to
unload.
   (B)   The driver must stay at the receiving location until the waste has
completely drained through the receiving station. The driver is responsible for
any spills or leaks from the truck during the evacuation of the waste at the
utility's designated waste receiving areas. Any hauling company that leaves the
waste receiving area in a condition unsatisfactory to the utility will be
required return to the treatment plant immediately to finish cleaning up the
station.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.08 SAFETY AND CONDUCT.
   (A)   Waste haulers, visitors, vendors, contractors, and outside company
representatives are expected to conduct business with the town Wastewater
Utility employees and/or on the facility premises in a professional, business-
like manner and follow the Wastewater Utility's safety requirements. Any
behavior contrary to this expectation will not be tolerated and the driver will
be asked to leave immediately. Unacceptable behavior may result in suspension
of the company's disposal privileges.
   (B)   The Director of the Wastewater Utility may suspend or revoke a hauling
company's dumping privileges at their discretion. Privileges may be suspended
or revoked for a variety of reasons, including, but not limited to, the
following: failure to comply with safety or conduct requirements, failure to
pay sewage billing fees in a timely manner, falsifying or omitting information
on a delivery confirmation receipt, illegal dumping, or other similar issues.
The Indiana Department of Environmental Management will be notified of any
company's suspension or revocation.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)
§ 54.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Additional enforcement proceedings for violations of the this chapter
may include the following penalties:
      (1)   First offense: $500 fine;
      (2)   Second offense: $1,000 fine;
      (3)   Third offense: license revoked.
   (B)   Any costs from enforcement or collections will be the responsibility
of the individual or company in violation.
(Ord. 2024-4-22(B), passed 4-22-2024)

CHAPTER 70: TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
Section
   
70.01   Authority
   
70.02   Definitions
   
70.03   Names of streets
   
70.04   Slow traffic lanes
   
70.05   Jake brakes
   
70.06   Loud or unnecessary noise
   
70.07   Proof of control
   
70.08   Enforcement authority
   
70.09   Oversized loads
 
   
70.99   Penalty
Editor’s note:
   This traffic code is based off of the following ordinances: Ord. III-A-1-a
(1), passed - -; Ord. III-A-1-a(2), passed 4-10-1995; Ord. III-A-1-a(6), passed
8-22-1983; Ord. III-A-1-a(1)-a, passed 8-3-1987; Ord. III-A-1-a(8), passed 4-
11-1994; Ord. III-A-1-a(10), passed 1-26-1996; Ord. III-A-1-a(11), passed 9-9-
1996; Ord. III-A-1-a(12), passed - -; Ord. III-A-1-a(13), passed 8-26-2002;
Ord. III-A-1-a(13)A, passed 3-25-2002; Ord. III-A-1-a(14), passed 9-23-2002;
Ord. III-A-1-a(15), passed 10-14-2002; Ord. III-A-1a(16), passed 2-24-2003;
Ord. III-A-1-a(17), passed 5-10-2004; Ord. 2004-9-13, passed 9-13-2004; Ord.
III-A-1-a(19), passed 11-29-2004; Ord. 2009-8-10, passed 8-10-2009; Ord. 2009-
10-12, passed 10-16-2009; Ord. 2010-12-13-D, passed 12-13-2010; Ord. III-A-1-a
(21)/2011-9-12, passed 9-26-2011; Ord. 2012-6-15, passed 6-18-2012; Ord. 2012-
3-12-C, passed 3-23-2012. Ordinances amending or revising any provision of this
traffic code passed later than the last ordinance in this list are placed
directly under corresponding sections herein.
§ 70.01 AUTHORITY.
   This traffic code is enacted pursuant to the provisions of I.C. 9-13-2-94,
9-21-1-1, 9-21-1-2, 9-21-1-3, 9-21-1-4, 9-21-1-5 and 9-21-4-3.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 1)
§ 70.02 DEFINITIONS.
   Words and phrases, when used in this traffic code, shall have their
ordinary, usual and customary meaning; except that, in case of conflict, the
statutory definitions contained in I.C. 9-13-2-1 et seq. shall prevail.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 2)
§ 70.03 NAMES OF STREETS.
   The street, alley and highway names hereafter used in this traffic code
shall be as shown on the recorded plats of the town on record in the Recorder’s
office in and for the county; except that, as to newly named streets, the plat
of said town drawn by E.T. Coy on 4-4-1969, incorporated herein by this
reference, and which is being filed with this traffic code in the records of
the town in the Clerk-Treasurer’s office shall be used to supplement same.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 3)
§ 70.04 SLOW TRAFFIC LANES.
   In the town, whenever a second or right-hand lane (not otherwise designated
as a turn lane) is available for travel, it shall be deemed a slow traffic
lane, and to the extent possible, so marked. Whenever a slow traffic lane is
available, it shall be unlawful for any vehicle, human powered, animal powered
or otherwise required to display a slow moving vehicle sign, to leave said lane
unless the reason is to overtake another such vehicle or emergency in nature.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 17) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.05 JAKE BRAKES.
   It shall be unlawful upon any road in or within 200 feet of a residential
zone within the town limits to apply a “Jake Brake” or similar engine brake
retarder device on a semi-tractor, tractor trailer combination or multi-axle
motor vehicle, or to utilize the engine to slow or reduce the speed of any said
vehicle or combination thereof so as to create a situation where the engine,
when utilized to slow said vehicle results in a loud noise emanating from said
vehicle.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 18) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.06 LOUD OR UNNECESSARY NOISE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle which make an unusually
loud or unnecessary noise, or which is not equipped with a muffler in constant
operation to prevent excessive or unusual noise or excessive smoke.
   (B)   It shall also be unlawful to operate a motor vehicle in a loud or
disorderly manner so as to disturb the peace and quiet of the residential
neighborhood.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 19) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.07 PROOF OF CONTROL.
   Unless the registered owner of a motor vehicle shall show that the operation
of the offending vehicle at the time and place of alleged offense was
unauthorized by him or her, the current motor vehicle registration of any
offending vehicle shall constitute prima facie proof that such person was in
control of the motor vehicle at the time of such violation.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 20)
§ 70.08 ENFORCEMENT AUTHORITY.
   (A)   The town shall have the right to direct the Town Marshal, or any other
agent, to remove or tow away, or to have removed or towed away by any
commercial towing serve any motor vehicle illegally parked pursuant to this
traffic code, or Ord. 79-4-2-A (now III-A), or any vehicle which blocks the use
of a fire hydrant, or may obstruct the movement of any emergency vehicle, or
where such parked vehicle creates or constitutes a traffic hazard or potential
traffic hazard. Any cars so towed away for illegal parking shall be stored in a
safe place and restored to the owner or operator of the same upon payment of
commercial towing service bill and a presentation of proper proof of ownership.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 21)
   (B)   (1)   The town is hereby authorized and directed to post signs, paint
signs on the pavement or otherwise notify vehicle operators of the existence of
this traffic code.
      (2)   Said employees are further directed to effectuate the provisions of
this traffic code as soon as same can be done.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 23)
§ 70.09 OVERSIZED LOADS.
   It shall be unlawful for any vehicle transporting a load which requires a
designation of oversized load, or a load which meets the definition of
oversized load as same may exist from time to time, and as defined by I.C.
Chapter 9, or any other Indiana Code concerning same, to utilize Fought Avenue
from Lake Avenue to the south town line for any purpose, said avenue being
restricted from utilization by units transporting such loads.
(Ord. 2020-5, passed 6-8-2019)
§ 70.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   (1)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the foregoing
provisions of this traffic code, or failing to obey any of the signs described
above and erected pursuant to same, or otherwise violating any of the portions
hereof shall be fined as follows:
         (a)   For Class A infractions: $100;
         (b)   For Class B infractions: $75;
         (c)   For Class C infractions: $50; and
         (d)   For Class D infractions: $25.
      (2)   Any subsequent admission or judgment of a violation thereafter of
the same ordinance or code provision within a calendar year shall be subject to
double the penalty set forth above as the total civil penalty, plus any and all
attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 24)
   (B)   Any person who violates the provisions of §
70.05 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s
fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 18)
   (C)   Any person who violates the provisions of §
70.06 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s
fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 19)
CHAPTER 71: PARKING RULES
Section
   
71.01   Definitions
   
71.02   Restricted parking
   
71.03   Overnight parking in parks
   
71.04   Moving parked cars
   
71.05   Public parking lots
 
   
71.99   Penalty
§ 71.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   PUBLIC PARKING LOT. Any parking lot owned or maintained by the town.
   PUBLIC STREET. Any street, including county roads, within the limits of the
town.
   VEHICLES. Automobiles, trucks, trailers, mobile homes, motor homes,
motorcycles and any other vehicles of any description designed to travel on two
or more wheels.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 4, § 1) (Ord. III-A-1-a(5), passed - -; Ord. III-A-1-
a(7), passed 1-24-1985)
§ 71.02 RESTRICTED PARKING.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle on a public street within the
town within 20 feet of the intersection of said public street and any other
public street.
   (B)   Any vehicle parked upon a public street, or in a public parking lot,
within the town shall be moved within 24 hours of the time of notice to do so
given to the owner of said vehicle by the Town Marshal.
   (C)   No vehicles shall be parked on any public street or on public property
within the town in such a manner as to obstruct the vision of drivers
approaching an intersection from any direction.
   (D)   Any vehicle parked on private property within the town in such a
manner as to obstruct the vision of drivers approaching an intersection from
any direction shall be moved upon notice to do so given to the owner of said
vehicle by the Town Marshal.
   (E)   It shall be unlawful to leave a motor vehicle or other vehicle of any
type on a town parking lot for more than 24 consecutive hours. If an individual
or business entity desires to leave a vehicle in a town parking lot for more
than 24 hours, that individual must apply to the Town Council and receive a
permit for same, and upon receipt of said permit, will be permitted to leave
said vehicle parking in the town parking lot for more than 24 consecutive
hours, so long as said permit is displayed in the windshield area of the
vehicle. Said permit must be applied for annually and shall be assessed a fee
of $25.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 4, § 2) (Ord. III-A-1-a(5), passed - -; Ord. III-A-1-
a(7), passed 1-24-1985; Ord. 2019-6-10, passed 6-10-2019) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.03 OVERNIGHT PARKING IN PARKS.
   No overnight parking shall be permitted in or upon any of the town-owned
parks, for non-park purposes on weekends, and there shall be no parking
absolute from 11:30 p.m. to 5:00 a.m., officer discretion to be exercised.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 5, § 1) (Ord. III-A-1-a(9), passed 8-14-1995)
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.04 MOVING PARKED CARS.
   It shall be unlawful for any individual to leave a motor vehicle parked upon
a town street in the town for a period in excess of two weeks without moving
said motor vehicle from any specific parking spot. It is the intent of this
section to require the movement of vehicles upon town streets so as to permit
routine maintenance, street cleaning and other necessary town functions which
cannot be accomplished by vehicles which sit for an inordinate amount of time
in a specific place.
(2013, Title IV, Ch. 6, § 1) (Ord. III-A-1-(a)(13), passed - -) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.05 PUBLIC PARKING LOTS.
   The town, through the office of the Town Marshal, is hereby authorized to
regulate the parking of vehicles and traffic on the property of Country Squire
Estates, Topeka Trace Apartments, Lake Bei Der Bank Apartments, West Edge
Apartments and other public parking lots located at businesses, churches and
schools.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 7) (Ord. III-A-1-a(8), passed 8-9-1993)
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   Any person violating the provisions of §
71.02(A) of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all
attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
      (2)   (a)   Any person violating the provisions of §
71.02(B) of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all
attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
         (b)   In addition to the fines for any infractions committed as listed
herein, any vehicle parked in violation of provisions of §
71.02(B) of this chapter shall be towed away at the owner’s expense.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 4, § 3)
      (3)   Any person violating the provisions of §
71.02(C) of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all
attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
      (4)   Any person violating the provisions of §
71.02(D) of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all
attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
      (5)   Any individual violating §
71.02(E) of this chapter shall have committed a Class B infraction and shall be
fined $50 for the first infraction and $100 for every violation of §
71.02(E) of this chapter thereafter. Any vehicle parked in violation of §
71.02(E) of this chapter may also be ordered towed by the Town Marshal, manager
or other town official, all at owner’s expense.
      (6)   Any subsequent admission or judgment of a violation thereafter of §
71.02 of this chapter or other code provision within a calendar year shall be
deemed a Class A infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an
amount not to exceed $100, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of
collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 4, § 2)
   (C)   (1)   Any person violating the provisions of §
71.03 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’
      (2)   Any subsequent admission or judgment of a violation thereafter of §
71.03 of this chapter within a calendar year shall be deemed a Class A
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to
exceed $100, plus any and all attorney’s fees, costs of collection and any
reasonable expenses incurred by the town.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 5, § 2)
   (D)   (1)   Any person violating the provisions of §
71.04 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s
fees, costs of collection and any expenses incurred by the town including, but
not limited to, towing and storage of said vehicle.
(2013, Title IV, Ch. 6, § 2)
      (2)   Any subsequent admission or judgment of a violation thereafter of §
71.04 of this chapter within a calendar year shall be deemed a Class A
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to
exceed $100, plus any and all attorney’s fees, costs of collection and any
other reasonable expenses incurred by the town.
(2013, Title IV, Ch. 6, § 3)
(Ord. III-A-1-a(5), passed - -; Ord. III-A-1-(a)(13), passed - -; Ord. III-A-1-
a(7), passed 1-24-1985; Ord. III-A-1-a(9), passed 8-14-1995; Ord. 2019-6-10,
passed 6-10-2019)
CHAPTER 72: SNOW EMERGENCIES
Section
   
72.01   Declaration of emergencies
   
72.02   Prohibited parking
   
72.03   Towing and moving vehicles
   
72.04   Enforcement procedures; notice
 
   
72.99   Penalty
§ 72.01 DECLARATION OF EMERGENCIES.
   The Town Council empowers the Town Manager to declare a snow emergency
within the corporate limits of the town at any time and from time to time as in
the complete discretion of said Town Manager may be necessary to secure the
orderly movement of traffic and removal of snow from the streets of the town.
Said declaration shall be announced to the public in such a manner as to inform
the largest number of residents of the town within the constraints of the
situation.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 8, § 1) (Ord. III-A-1-d(7), passed 12-3-1984)
§ 72.02 PROHIBITED PARKING.
   Upon the declaration of a snow emergency, no vehicle shall be parked, remain
parked or be left standing on any uncleared portion of Lake Street from the
west corporate limits of the town to the east corporate limits of the town, nor
on Main Street from the north corporate limits of the town to south corporate
limits of the town.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 8, § 2) (Ord. III-A-1-d(7), passed 12-3-1984)
Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.03 TOWING AND MOVING VEHICLES.
   The town shall have the right to direct the Town Marshal or any other agents
to remove and tow away, or have removed and towed away, by any commercial
towing service, any motor vehicle illegally parked under this chapter. Any
motor vehicle so towed away shall be stored in a safe place and restored to the
owner or operator of the same upon the payment of the commercial towing bill,
presentation of proper proof of ownership and proof of payment of the penalty
under this chapter.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 8, § 3) (Ord. III-A-1-d(7), passed 12-3-1984)
§ 72.04 ENFORCEMENT PROCEDURES; NOTICE.
   (A)   (1)   Whenever the Town Marshal or any duly qualified and acting law
enforcement officer shall find that any person has committed any action which
is declared unlawful by the provisions of this chapter, such Marshal or officer
may give written notice to such person of such violation. All such notices
shall be serially numbered and shall contain the following information:
         (a)   The specific violation with which the violator is charged;
         (b)   The location of the violation;
         (c)   The signature of the Marshal or officer;
         (d)   The date of the violation; and
         (e)   The amount of penalty prescribed by §
72.99 of this chapter.
      (2)   The notice shall also contain the following statement: “Within 72
hours from the time of violation as shown on this notice of violation, bring
this notice to the Clerk-Treasurer’s office, Town Hall, Topeka, Indiana, 46571,
or mail fine to such address within 72 hours from the time of violation or
warrant will be issued for arrest which may result in extra costs.”
      (3)   All such written notices shall be executed by the Town Marshal or
officer in triplicate. One copy shall be served upon the violator as herein
provided, one copy shall be filed in the office of the Town Marshal and one
copy with the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
   (B)   Any person receiving written notice of a violation pursuant to the
provisions of this chapter shall, within 72 hours from the date of the
violation, appear at the Clerk-Treasurer’s office, Town Hall, Topeka, Indiana,
46571, and pay the prescribed penalty, by depositing such amount along with the
notice of violation with the officer on duty or in the place provided and
marked for such purpose, or such person within such time may mail such fine
with the written notice to the Clerk-Treasurer’s office. In the event that said
72-hour period shall expire on Saturday, Sunday or legal holiday, such violator
shall have up to 4:00 p.m. on the next day following that the Clerk-Treasurer’s
office is open. The penalties which shall be payable in compromise of the
violations of this chapter shall be in accordance herewith.
   (C)   If any person receiving notice of violation shall fail to appear to
pay the penalty for such violation, under this chapter within the prescribed
time, the Town Marshal shall prepare or cause to be prepared a proper affidavit
for the arrest of such violator. Procedures for arrest and court appearance
shall be in accordance with I.C. 34-28-5-1 et seq. Each arrest summons shall be
docketed in the County or Circuit Court of the county, in the name of the town
pursuant to law and the rules and regulations of said court. It shall be the
duty of the attorney representing the town or said attorney’s delegate (which
delegate may be the prosecuting attorney) to prosecute each violation of this
chapter.
   (D)   The County Clerk shall remit fines collected for violation of this
chapter into the General Fund of the town by transmittal to the Town Clerk-
Treasurer not less often than monthly. The County Clerk shall distribute costs
in accordance with the statutory schedules.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 8, § 5) (Ord. III-A-1-d(7), passed 12-3-1984)
§ 72.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who violates the provisions of this chapter commits a Class C
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to
exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees, costs of collection and any
reasonable expenses incurred by the town in connection with removing and
storage of said vehicle.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 8, § 4) (Ord. III-A-1-d(7), passed 12-3-1984)
CHAPTER 73: RECREATIONAL VEHICLES
Section
Golf Carts
   
73.01   Definitions
   
73.02   Operation of golf carts
   
73.03   Operator requirements; financial responsibility
   
73.04   Time and place of operation
   
73.05   Occupants
   
73.06   Traffic rules
   
73.07   Slow-moving vehicle sign
 
   
73.99   Penalty
GOLF CARTS
§ 73.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DRIVER’S LICENSE. A valid license to operate a motor vehicle issued by
Indiana or any other state.
   FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY. Liability insurance coverage on a golf cart in an
amount not less than required by state law for motor vehicles operated on
public highways in the state.
   GOLF CART. A vehicle originally designed for operation on a golf course and
powered by a battery or internal combustion motor.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 1) (Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009)
§ 73.02 OPERATION OF GOLF CARTS.
   The operation of a golf cart within the town is strictly prohibited unless
the golf cart is operated, insured and equipped in full compliance with this
subchapter.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 2) (Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009) Penalty,
see §
73.99
§ 73.03 OPERATOR REQUIREMENTS; FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY.
   (A)   Only persons over 16 years of age and holding a valid driver’s license
may operate a golf cart.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 3)
   (B)   The operator or owner of a golf cart must show financial
responsibility when operating a golf cart. Written proof of financial
responsibility must be available on the golf cart or carried by the operator at
all times.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 4)
(Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.04 TIME AND PLACE OF OPERATION.
   (A)   Golf carts shall not be operated on any town streets between one-half
hour after sunset and one-half hour before sunrise, unless the golf cart is
equipped with two operating headlights (one on each side of the front of the
golf cart), and two operating tail lights with brake lights and turn signals
(one on each side of the rear of the golf cart), which are visible from a
distance of 500 feet.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 5)
   (B)   Golf carts may be operated on town streets, alleys and parking lots.
Golf carts may not be operated on sidewalks.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 6)
(Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.05 OCCUPANTS.
   The number of occupants in a golf cart shall be limited to the number of
persons for whom factory seating is installed and provided on the golf cart;
provided, no more than four persons shall occupy any cart. The operator and all
occupants shall be seated in the golf cart and no parts of the bodies of the
operator or any occupant shall extend outside the perimeter of the golf cart
while the golf cart is being operated.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 7) (Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009) Penalty,
see §
73.99
§ 73.06 TRAFFIC RULES.
   The operator of the golf cart shall comply with all traffic rules and
regulations adopted by the state and the town which govern the operation of
motor vehicles.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 8) (Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009) Penalty,
see §
73.99
§ 73.07 SLOW-MOVING VEHICLE SIGN.
   All golf carts must display on the back of the golf cart a “slow-moving
vehicle” sign of the same type required under state law.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 9) (Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009) Penalty,
see §
73.99
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   A violation of any provision of §§
73.01 through
73.07 of this chapter shall constitute a Class A infraction and a violation of
this code of ordinances. An owner, lessee or operator may be cited to appear in
a court of competent jurisdiction by issuance of a state uniform traffic
ticket. Upon finding by such court than an owner, lessee or operator of a golf
cart has violated any provision of §§
73.01 through
73.07 of this chapter, such person shall be subject to a fine not to exceed
$100, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection for each
offense, along with court costs.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 9, § 10) (Ord. 2009-6-8A, passed 6-8-2009)
CHAPTER 74: PLAYGROUND ALLEY
Section
   
74.01   Naming
   
74.02   One-way traffic
   
74.03   No parking
   
74.04   Registration; authorization
   
74.05   Moving or towing vehicle
   
74.06   Violation
 
   
74.99   Penalty
§ 74.01 NAMING.
   The unnamed alley which is located immediately east of and parallel to
Harrison Street, which runs in a north and south direction from School Street,
extended to South Alley shall henceforth and hereafter be known as “Playground
Alley”.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 1) (Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -)
§ 74.02 ONE-WAY TRAFFIC.
   One-way traffic signs shall be erected at the intersection of School Street
extended and along Playground Alley, and that all motorists shall be obligated
to operate their motor vehicles, in compliance with same, viz: one-way traffic
north bound, between School Street extended and South Alley for the entire
length of Playground Alley.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 2) (Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -) Penalty, see
§
74.99
§ 74.03 NO PARKING.
   No parking signs shall be erected and no parking shall be allowed and all
motorists shall be obligated to operate their motor vehicles in such a manner
so as not to violate same, viz: on both sides of Playground Alley, between
School Street extended and South Alley.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 3) (Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -) Penalty, see
§
74.99
§ 74.04 REGISTRATION; AUTHORIZATION.
   The current motor vehicle registration of any offending vehicle shall
constitute prima facie proof that such person was in control of the motor
vehicle at the time of such violation; however, said registered owner shall
have the right to rebut said presumption by proving that said use at the time
and place was unauthorized by him or her.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 4) (Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -)
§ 74.05 MOVING OR TOWING VEHICLE.
   The town shall have the right to direct the Town Marshal or any other agents
to remove and tow away, or have removed or towed away, by any commercial towing
service, any motor vehicle illegally parked upon or along either side of
Playground Alley. Any vehicles so towed away for illegal parking shall be
stored in a safe place and restored to the owner or operator of same upon
payment of a commercial towing service bill and the presentation or proper
proof of ownership.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 5) (Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -)
§ 74.06 VIOLATION.
   (A)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the aforesaid
provisions of this chapter or failing to obey any of the signs described above
erected pursuant to same or to otherwise violate any of the portions hereof
shall be treated in accordance with this traffic code previously enacted by the
Town Council.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 6)
   (B)   The second admission or judgment of a violation of this chapter within
a calendar year shall be subject to double the penalty set forth above as the
total civil penalty. Any third admission or judgment of a violation of the same
ordinance or code provision within a calendar year shall be subject to triple
the penalty set forth above as the total civil penalty.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 7)
(Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -)
§ 74.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any owner or operator of a vehicle violating the provisions of §
74.02 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s
fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 2)
   (B)   Any person who violates the provisions of §
74.03 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s
fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 2, § 3)
(Ord. III-A-1-a(3), passed - -)

SCHEDULE II. WEIGHT AND LENGTH LIMITS.
   (A)   The use of a tractor-mobile home rig, having a combined overall length
in excess of 60 feet, within the corporate limits of the town shall be limited
to the following streets: C.R. 700 W; Hawpatch Street; Main Street; Lake
Street; Michigan Street; and North Street; provided, however, that, other
streets in said town may be used if it is necessary to use the same to install
a mobile home in said town for residential purposes, and written permission of
the Town Marshal is first obtained.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 22)
   (B)   In the town, there shall be no truck plated 13,000 pounds or more
permitted on the first alley south of Lake Street, beginning at a point 90 feet
west of South Harrison Street and continuing to the elementary school.
(Ord. 2017-9-25(C), passed 9-25-2017)
Penalty, see §
70.99

SCHEDULE IV. SPEED LIMITS.
   The following speed zones are hereby established, and shall be marked with
appropriate signs. No motorist shall drive faster than is permitted by this
schedule in the following zones.
   (A)   “Speed Zone Ahead” signs shall be erected approaching the corporate
limits on: East Lake Street; West Lake Street; Hawpatch Street, approaching
north corporate limits; and Main Street, approaching the south corporate
limits.
   (B)   Unless otherwise provided by this schedule, or by subsequent
ordinance, the speed limit on all streets, roads and highway within the
corporate limits of the town shall be 30 mph. Signs indicating this 30 mph
speed limit shall be erected at: the intersection of West Lake Street and the
Redman Drive; at the intersection of East Lake Street and the east property
limits of Topeka Livestock Auction, Inc. at the intersection of the north
corporate limits and Hawpatch; and at the intersection of the south corporate
limits and Main Street. Any person who violates the provisions of this division
(B) commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined
in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of
collection.
   (C)   During school hours, signs shall be erected at Mill Street,
approaching from the north on Main Street, and at Pine Street, approaching from
the south on Main Street, which signs shall indicate “School Zone” and “20 mph
Speed Zone”. Any person who violates the provisions of this division (C)
commits a Class B infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an
amount not to exceed $75, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of
collection.
   (D)   The speed zone on West Lake Street, between the west corporate limits
and Redman Drive, and on East Lake Street, between the east corporate limits
and the east property line of Topeka Livestock Auction, Inc., is hereby
established at 40 mph, and signs indicating this speed limit shall be erected
at the west corporation limit on West Lake Street and at the east corporation
limits on East Lake Street. Any person who violates the provisions of this
division (D) commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof,
be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and
costs of collection.
   (E)   The speed zone on Pleasant Drive is hereby reduced to 20 mph, and
signs indicating this speed limit shall be erected in appropriate and lawful
positions thereon. Any person who violates the provisions of this division (E)
commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an
amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of
collection.
   (F)   The entire length of Nature Trail shall be posted a 25 mph speed
limit. Any person who violates the provisions of this division (F) commits a
Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount
not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
   (G)   The speed limit on Hawpatch Drive and Lehman Avenue shall be 35 mph.
Any person who violates the provisions of this division (G) commits a Class C
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to
exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
   (H)   The speed limit on School Street, from South Main Street to Harrison
Street, shall be posted a 20 mph speed limit. Any person who violates the
provisions of this division (H) commits a Class B infraction and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $75, plus any and all
attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
   (I)   In the town, the speed limit for North Street, in both directions from
its intersection with North Main Street to its intersection with Pleasant
Avenue, shall be posted 20 mph. Any person who violates the provisions of this
division (I) commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof,
be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and
costs of collection.
   (J)   In the town, the speed limit for Harrison Street, in both directions
from School Street to North Street shall be posted a 20 mph school zone. Any
person who violates the provisions of this division (J) commits a Class B
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to
exceed $75, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
   (K)   In the town, the speed limit for the area known as “Golden Acres”,
which includes North Golden Drive, South Golden Drive, Jay Street, Todd Street
and Meadow Lane, shall have a speed limit established at 20 mph. Any person who
violates the provisions of this division (K) commits a Class C infraction and
shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus
any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
   (L)   In the town, the speed limit for Crossfire Drive shall be posted 20
mph.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 4) (Ord. 2015-11-23(C), passed 11-23-2015)
CHAPTER 76: PARKING SCHEDULES
Schedule
      
I.   Restricted and prohibited parking
SCHEDULE I. RESTRICTED AND PROHIBITED PARKING.
   (A)   No vehicle shall be parked on Lake Street or on Main Street within the
town, between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m., except for that part of
Lake Street between Harrison Street and Pleasant Avenue, upon which parking
shall be allowed on an alternate basis, on the north side on even numbered
calendar days and on the south side on odd numbered calendar days of said
street, on alternate days. This provision is intended to promote the public
necessity of street sweeping for Lake Street and Main Street within the town.
Any person violating the provisions of this division (A) commits a Class C
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not to
exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 4, § 2E)
   (B)   “No Parking Here to Corner” signs shall be erected in accordance with
this traffic code. Any person who violates the provisions of this division (B)
commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an
amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of
collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 11)
   (C)   (1)   “No Parking this Side of Street” signs shall be erected in the
following areas:
         (a)   On the east side of Main Street, between School Street and Mill
Street;
         (b)   On the west side of Hawpatch Street, from Amish Alley to Roy
Street;
         (c)   On the west side of Main Street, from Pine Street to Indiana
Street;
         (d)   On both sides of Pleasant Drive, from Amish Alley to Lake
Street;
         (e)   On the west side of South Main Street, beginning at the south
end of the driveway at 128 South Main Street and continuing to the north side
of School Street;
         (f)   On the west side of north Harrison Street, beginning from the
south at East Lake Street and continuing to the north of East North Street;
         (g)   On the south side of East Mill Street, beginning from the east
at South Main Street and continuing to the west at South Harrison Street;
         (h)   On the east side of North Babcock Street, beginning at West Lake
Street and continuing to the north, ending at Amish Alley; and
         (i)   On the north and south sides of Crossfire Drive, between Zook
Street and South Main Street.
      (2)   Any person who violates the provisions of this division (C) commits
a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount
not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 12)
   (D)   In the town, on the north side of North Street from North Main Street
east to the alley shall be posted as a no parking zone. The town is hereby
authorized and directed to post signs, paint signs on the pavement, or
otherwise notify vehicle operators of the existence of this division (D). Said
employees are further directed to effectuate the provisions of this division
(D) as soon as same can be done. Any person who violates the provisions of this
division (D) commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof,
be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s fees and
costs of collection.
(2013 Code, Title IV, Ch. 1, § 13)
   (E)   In the town, there shall be no parking on the west side of South
Harrison Street from the intersection with Mill Street north to the alley
running east and west.
   (F)   In the town, there shall be no parking on the north and south sides of
Crossfire Drive, between Zook Street and South Main Street.
   (G)   In the town, there shall be no parking from 12:00 a.m. to 7:00 a.m.
on: the north and south sides of East Lake Street, from its intersection with
Main Street to the town limits; the east and west sides of South Main Street,
from its intersection with Lake Street to the town limits; and the east side of
Main Street from its intersection with Lake Street to Roy Street.
   (H)    In the town, on North Street, on the south side, from Merchants
Alley, going west to North Main Street, the first three parking spots shall be
designated as handicapped spots, and the remaining space adjoining North Street
shall be designated as no parking.
   (I)   The first three parking spots on the south side of North Street east
of the intersection with North Main shall become loading zone, no parking.
   (J)   There shall be no parking on either side of Todd Street, from Jay to
the cul de sac.
(Ord. 2014-7-28, passed 7-28-2014; Ord. 2015-10-26(b), passed 10-26-2015; Ord.
2016-8-8, passed 8-8-2016; Ord. 2018-10-22(A), passed 10-22-2018; Ord. 2020-8,
passed 8-10-2020; Ord. 2020-10A, passed 11-23-2020)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 HORSES.
   (A)   (1)   No horses or other large animals shall be permitted within
portions of the town, which have previously been subdivided into lots that do
not contain at least two acres of designated pasture.
      (2)   The pasture necessary to maintain a horse in the town shall be two
acres’ minimum of designated pasture for no more than two horses. For each
additional horse, there will need to be an additional one acre of designated
pasture. Designated pasture shall not include lawns, other areas adjacent to
the living quarters or structures. Pasture areas and horses shall be maintained
so that any smells shall not leave the site and effluent shall be kept clean
from said site and not permitted to leave said site during rainstorms or other
times, nor be stored anywhere near or upon the pasture lines. It is intended
that the responsible homeowner shall maintain said horse and pasture in a way
that is not inconsistent with town living, nor creating a hazard or nuisance
for any neighbor.
   (B)   (1)   An individual shall file with the town a petition in writing
requesting that he or she be permitted horses and/or large animals, pursuant to
division (A) above.
      (2)   Said written request shall include a drawing, which shall clearly
delineate the designated pasture area, which shall be at least two acres and
comply fully with all requirements of this division (B), including any area for
which waste shall be accumulated and any shelters.
      (3)   Following the filing of said petition and drawing, the Town Manager
shall inspect said property to ascertain compliance with division (A) above,
specifically ascertaining the existence of a designated pasture, and shall
report to the Town Council his or her findings and recommendations.
      (4)   Following the report to the Town Council, the Town Council shall
make a determination, said determination shall be reduced to writing, and shall
be forwarded to the county’s Plan Commission for use at the Topeka-Wolcottville
BZA hearing. The letter issued by the Town Board as concerns said pasture shall
be a recommendation to said BZA and reference division (A)’s requirements.
(Ord. 2018.5.14(B), passed 5-14-2018; Ord. 2018-6-11(C), passed 6-11-2018)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.02 LARGE ANIMALS PULLING CARTS AND THE LIKE.
   The Town Council requests that the County Commission and Council require,
through law, the installation and use of “horse diapers” on all animal-drawn
devices that are intended and used for road and street purposes.
(Ord. 2015-9-28(B), passed 9-28-2015)
§ 90.03 4-H ANIMAL PERMITS.
   (A)   An animal permit is required for a child to house and care for any 4-
H animal within the town limits that is otherwise prohibited pursuant to the
applicable town ordinance (horse, calf, swine, goat and sheep).
   (B)   (1)   In order to apply for a 4-H animal permit, an interested party
must request a hearing before the Town Council.
      (2)   In making a determination, the Council will take into account the
following factors which must be provided by the party seeking the 4-H animal
permit:
         (a)   Size of the lot in which the animal will be kept or otherwise
cared for;
         (b)   Type of shelter or accommodations necessary for housing said
animal;
         (c)   Type of animal, including:
            1.   Size;
            2.   Characteristics; and
            3.   Temperament.
         (d)   Child’s past experience or skill in raising or caring for said
animals; and
         (e)   The town will notify all adjacent neighbors for input.
   (C)   The permit must be renewed annually if the child wishes to continue
participation in 4-H activities with said animal; there is no fee for the
permit or renewal.
(2013 Code, Title V, Ch. 20) (Ord. 2013-9-9(A), passed - -2013)
§ 90.04 DOGS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any owner to allow any dog owned by him or
her to stray beyond said owner’s premises unless said dog is on a leash or is
under the reasonable control of some person, such dog is hereby declared a
public nuisance.
   (B)   Any dog running at large upon the streets or alleys or public places
in the town, unless said dog is on a leash or under the reasonable control of
some person, such dog is subject to being killed without notice by the Town
Marshal or by a duly appointed employee of said town.
(Title V, Ch. 6) (Ord. III-C-1-a(1), passed - -) Penalty, see §
90.99
PET WASTE
§ 90.15 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to establish requirements for the proper
disposal of pet solid waste in the town, so as to protect public health, safety
and welfare, and to prescribe penalties for failure to comply.
(Ord. 2018-02-26(B), passed 2-26-2018)
§ 90.16 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning. When not
inconsistent with the context, words used in the present tense include the
future, words used in the plural number include the singular number, and words
used in the singular number include the plural number. The word “shall” is
always mandatory and not merely directory.
   IMMEDIATE. The pet solid waste is removed at once, without delay.
   OWNER/KEEPER. Any person who shall possess, maintain, house or harbor any
pet or otherwise have custody of any pet, whether or not the owner of such pet.
   PERSON. Any individual, corporation, company, partnership, firm, association
or political subdivision of the state subject to municipal jurisdiction.
   PET. A domesticated animal (other than a disability assistance animal) kept
for amusement or companionship, including, but not limited to, dogs, cats or
pet pigs.
   PET SOLID WASTE. Waste matter expelled from the bowels of the pet;
excrement.
   PROPER DISPOSAL. Placement in a designated waste receptacle, or other
suitable container, and discarded in a refuse container which is regularly
emptied by the municipality or some other refuse collector; or disposal into a
system designed to convey domestic sewage for proper treatment and disposal.
   REMOVAL EQUIPMENT. Any tool, implement or other device carried for the
purpose of picking up and contain pet waste.
(Ord. 2018-02-26(B), passed 2-26-2018)
§ 90.17 DISPOSAL REQUIREMENT; REMOVAL EQUIPMENT.
   (A)   All pet owners and keepers are required to immediately and properly
dispose of their pets’ solid waste deposited on any property, public or
private, not owned or possessed by that person, absent the owner’s consent.
   (B)   All pet owners and keepers are required to possess means of removal of
their pets’ solid pet waste at all times while present with said pet on any
property, public or private, not owned or possessed by that person, absent the
owner’s consent.
(Ord. 2018-02-26(B), passed 2-26-2018) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.18 EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   Any owner or keeper who requires the use of a disability assistance
service animal shall be exempt from the provisions of this subchapter while
such animal is being used for that purpose. This exemption does not apply to
therapy animals and/or emotional support animals.
   (B)   On-duty law enforcement officers operating with K-9 animals shall also
be exempt from the provisions of this subchapter while such personnel and
animal are engaged in law enforcement duty.
(Ord. 2018-02-26(B), passed 2-26-2018)
§ 90.19 ENFORCEMENT.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall be enforced by the Town Marshal.
(Ord. 2018-02-26(B), passed 2-26-2018)
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person violating §
90.01 of this chapter commits a Class A infraction for each day of said
violation and shall be assessed $100 for each such day, as well as attorney’s
fees and costs incurred by the town as a result of said violation.
   (C)   Any person who violates the provisions of §
90.04 of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $50, plus any and all attorney’s
fees and costs of collection.
(Title V, Ch. 6)
   (D)   (1)   Any person violating the provisions of §§
90.15 through
90.19 of this chapter commits a Class D infraction and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined in an amount not to exceed $25, plus any and all attorney’s
fees and costs of collection.
      (2)   Any subsequent violation thereafter within a calendar year shall be
subject to double the penalty set forth above as the total civil penalty, plus
any and all attorney’s fees and costs of collection.
(Ord. III-C-1-a(1), passed - -; Ord. 2018-02-26(B), passed 2-26-2018; Ord.
2018.5.14(B), passed 5-14-2018)
